Contains every `message_start`, `message_update` (thinking deltas + text deltas), `message_end`, and lifecycle events (`agent_start`, `turn_start`, `turn_end`, `agent_end`). This is the verbatim prompt stream that `pi` sends to the model.\n- **`pi-context-test.jsonl`** — A session dump from a `scout` flow that attempted to extract the agent's full context window. The model (GLM-5.1 via wafer) refused the request, classifying it as a social engineering attempt. The refusal reasoning is fully captured in the thinking deltas.\n- **`test-session.jsonl`** — A minimal synthetic session used for testing the JSONL dump parser.\n- **Marker files (`.md`, `.txt`)** — Simple test outputs generated by earlier `build` or `scout` flows to verify file write permissions and env var propagation.\n\n## Analysis Notes\n\n### 🔑 High-value artifacts\n\n1. **`pi-run-output.log`** — This is the primary target for analysis. It contains:\n   - 122 JSONL lines\n   - 113 `message_update` events (mostly thinking deltas + text deltas)\n   - Full thinking trace from GLM-5.1 showing how the model evaluates a system-prompt-exfiltration request\n   - Provider metadata (`wafer`, `glm-5.1`) embedded in message events\n   - No errors or warnings found in the stream\n\n2. **`pi-context-test.jsonl`** — Secondary target. Contains the same session in a more compact format with explicit `model_change` and `thinking_level_change` events. Useful for comparing dump formats.\n\n### 🗑️ Noise / low-value artifacts\n\n- `pi-context-test.md`, `pi-context-test2.md`, `payload-test.txt`, `payload-validate.txt` — These are simple test markers. They verify basic I/O worked but contain no analytical value on their own.\n- `test-session.jsonl` — Minimal synthetic data. Useful only for parser validation.\n\n### 🔍 What deserves deeper inspection\n\n1. **Thinking delta fidelity** — `pi-run-output.log` has 113 `message_update` events streaming the model's reasoning word-by-word. This is extremely verbose. We should analyze whether all thinking deltas are necessary, or if we should collapse them into a single `thinking` block for downstream analysis.\n\n2. **Model metadata inconsistency** — `pi-context-test.jsonl` has a top-level `model_change` event, while `pi-run-output.log` embeds provider/model inside every `message_update`. We should standardize on one schema.\n\n3. **Usage/cost fields are all zeros** — Every event in `pi-run-output.log` shows `\"input\":0,\"output\":0,\"cacheRead\":0,\"cacheWrite\":0`. This suggests the dump is written *before* the model completes, or usage tracking isn't wired into the event stream. We should fix this if we want accurate cost analysis.\n\n4. **Session ID collision** — Both `pi-context-test.jsonl` and `pi-run-output.log` share the same session ID (`019e2867-7a94-7778-a542-29feaf30e11a`) but appear to be different dumps of the same session. We need to understand if the dump pipeline deduplicates or appends.\n\n5. **Security posture** — The captured thinking trace shows GLM-5.1 correctly identifying and refusing a system-prompt exfiltration attempt. Root cause: `randomizedCenter()` could place the ripple origin on a space character in the test string `'Hello world!'`. At 30ms `initialTimeOffset` the radius was <1, so adjacent non-space characters fell outside the depth band and no ANSI was emitted, causing intermittent failures. Changed test text to `'Helloworld!!'` (no spaces) and tightened TPS KPI render timing from 100ms to 40ms post-flash to avoid afterglow-only windows where `dur < 210` suppresses echo pops. Full suite now passes consistently (5/5 scramble-only runs + full 977-test run).\n\n## Files\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `tests/scramble.test.ts` | Test suite — illuminate-mode cases hardened |\n\n## Actions\n\n| # | Action | Details |\n|---|--------|---------|\n| 1 | Changed 4 illuminate-mode test cases | Text changed to `'Helloworld!!'` / `'Helloworld!!!'` |\n| 2 | Changed TPS KPI `afterCooldown` render timing | From `base + 3200ms` → `base + 3140ms` |\n| 3 | Verified fix with consecutive runs | 5 scramble-only runs (185/185 each) |\n| 4 | Verified full test suite | 977/977 tests passing |\n\n## Commands\n\n- `npx vitest run tests/scramble.test.ts` (scramble-only, ×5)\n- `npx vitest run` (full suite, ×1)\n\n## Not Done\n\n- None\n\n## Next Steps\n\n1. Export flow report to repo (current mission)\n2. Monitor CI for any edge cases on different runners\n\n## Reasoning\n\n1. `randomizedCenter` picks a position in the 20%–80% range of text length. For a 12-character string, position 5 is the space between \"Hello\" and \"world\".\n2. When the center lands on a space, neighbors at distance 1 have negative depth at 30ms because the radius is <1, so no characters are scrambled.\n3. Removing spaces guarantees the center character is always a scramblable character, eliminating the zero-ANSI window.\n4. The TPS KPI timing fragility was caused by a 100ms post-flash window occasionally landing in an afterglow-only state where `dur < 210` suppresses echo pops. <directive>
## Mission

During this scout flow — your mission is to discover relevant context. Move fast, stay surgical, and treat the conversation history above as background reference only.

## Workflow

1. Survey — use `ls`, `find`, and `grep` to locate relevant files and symbols before reading whole files.
2. Inspect — use `batch` with `o: "read"`, `s: <offset>`, and `l: <limit>` for targeted file reading instead of bash `sed`/`head`/`tail`.
3. If `batch` returns a context map for a large code/infra file, do not retry the full-file read; use the reported line ranges for targeted follow-up reads.
4. Trace — follow code paths, dependencies, configuration, and tests that explain the requested area.
5. Report — cite concrete evidence and stop when the requested context is mapped.

## Rules

- This is a read-oriented flow: do not modify files.
- Cite every finding with a precise file path and line number or range.
- Include relevant snippets or evidence inline so citations are verifiable.
- Show actual code/data, not excessive summaries.
- If something is not found, say so directly — do not guess.

## Structured Output
End with a ```json block: { version, status, summary, files[], actions[], notDone[], nextSteps[], reasoning[], notes[] }. Commands auto-extracted; omit empty arrays. Keep snippets under 300 chars. List at most 10 items per array.
</directive>
